Women Advocate for Domestic Goods

Inaugural Meeting Held Yesterday

Executive and Supervisory Committee Members Elected

The Shanghai Women's Association for the Promotion of Domestic Goods held its inaugural meeting at the City General Chamber of Commerce at 2 p.m. yesterday. More than one hundred people attended, including Mayor Zhang Qun, Zhu Yakui representing the City Party Department, Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Social Affairs Bureau, Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Ye Huijun, Wang Jiean, Dong Keren from the City General Chamber of Commerce, and various members. The meeting was chaired by Ms. Ma Yuying, Tang Guanyu, and Lin Kecong, recorded by Tang Naixin, and emceed by Chen Jingrong. The meeting was conducted in a formal and orderly manner. First, Chairperson Ma Yuying delivered the opening remarks and reported on the preparations and the origins of the Women's Association for the Promotion of Domestic Goods. Then, Zhu Yakui representing the City Party Department, Mayor Zhang, and the Director of the Social Affairs Bureau delivered speeches (details omitted). Ye Huijun, Wang Xiaolai, and others followed with speeches (details omitted). Next, the articles of association were discussed, revised, and passed. Then, eleven executive committee members, five supervisory committee members, and five alternate executive committee members were elected.

Page 14

Three alternate supervisory committee members were elected. The declaration was passed, and the executive and supervisory committee members were sworn into office. Tea and refreshments were served, and photos were taken before the meeting adjourned.

Elected Officials:

Eleven Executive Committee Members: Lin Kecong, Xu Shuzhen, Tang Guanyu, Ouyang Yawen, Han Jingnong, Zheng Shen, Zhou Yanghao, Mrs. Jin Wensi, Ying Yining, Ding Lude, Tang Naixin.

Five Alternates: Chen Hongbi, Chen Jingrong, Ding Shuying, Jin Suqin, Wu Ruoan.

Five Supervisory Committee Members: Ma Yuying, Jiang Zhangchu, Wang Xiaoying, Liang Longguang, Shu Huizhen.

Three Alternates: Li Jingjuan, Ge Jinghe, Ma Fengqi.

Declaration of the General Assembly:

Declaration of the Inaugural Meeting of the Shanghai Women's Association for the Promotion of Domestic Goods

Since the preparation of this association, we have deeply relied on the efforts of the founders to solicit comrades, and after several discussions, the framework has been roughly established. The general assembly is thus established. Coinciding with the beginning of national unification, peace, and construction, colleagues feel that the national duty cannot be abandoned, and resolutely take on the responsibility of promoting domestic goods. We hereby list the three aspects of our future efforts for our female compatriots:

(1) To promote domestic goods, we should arouse deep understanding and adhere to it permanently, and not leave the criticism of a five-minute enthusiasm. In the past, the movement to promote domestic goods has been surging, no less than the excitement of stimulating nerves. If it loses its effect, some intellectuals with weak national consciousness will criticize it as useless to promote domestic goods without making efforts to produce. This statement seems right but is not, because it is hoped that those who are in a semi-colonial status will make every effort to exclude foreign goods, so that domestic goods can be developed. According to the teachings of the President Sun Yat-sen, only by knowing and uniting with the group can we revitalize the national spirit and solve the people's livelihood. Today, this association will reveal the facts of foreign economic aggression as much as possible, so that our female compatriots will be awe-inspiring in the life and death of the nation and will strive to reduce the fierce flames of foreign goods in the market. This is the first goal that this association aims to strive for.

(2) To promote the use of domestic goods, we must set an example and create a trend. For decades, foreign goods have gradually formed a deep and unshakable foundation in the Chinese market, even reaching remote areas. Almost all of the necessities of life, clothing, food, and daily use, are supplied by foreign goods. The reason for this is not only due to the deliberate efforts of imperialists to hold special forces and carry out economic oppression, but also due to the depression of the national spirit, the loss of self-confidence, and the psychology of worshiping foreign goods and despising domestic goods in our country. Consider, my female compatriots in Shanghai, it is undeniable that there are many who love beauty, keep up with the times, and compete with each other to pursue luxury and desire and love foreign goods. The trend is so strong throughout the country! However, living in a foreign country, I have seen desolate borders and starving compatriots, who are being exploited by foreign goods. We should consider the difficulty of building a new country and the fact that the entire nation has not been freed from shackles. From now on, we should break the boat and completely ban imported luxury goods. Even if there are domestic goods available for daily use, we must not buy foreign goods again. We should swear to be sincere and establish it as a creed. From oneself and one's family, we should extend it to the society and encourage each other to abide by it without change, in order to change the trend and turn the public will into a city. However, what should be stated here is that this kind of movement is by no means out of a negative thought of restraining desire. We firmly believe that the enjoyment of materials must be based on one's own creation. If there is no contribution to the international community, but only to use the blood and sweat of compatriots to exchange for the boasting of the civilization of life, it is a shameful act of stagnation. We hope that the talented and wise men of the country will strive to create material civilization, reap one point and enjoy one point, be down-to-earth and not be involved in emptiness. This is the second goal that this association aims to strive for.

(3) To strive to promote domestic goods and state opinions on improving manufacturing. In recent years, the domestic goods industry has made considerable progress, and the necessary daily necessities are largely complete. Unfortunately, it has not been able to produce in large quantities, and sometimes the excellent quality cannot be maintained permanently. In the future, this association will strive to promote the excellent domestic goods, promote their production and sales, and promote their advantages and expand them. Even for inferior products, we will not hesitate to point them out truthfully and hope that industrialists will step up their improvements. As for the fundamental plan for developing domestic goods, we should discuss and study the one-sided views and contribute them to the party and government authorities and the industrial and commercial sectors for adoption. We also plan to contact domestic goods manufacturers from time to time to hold exhibitions of various clothing, food, household goods, etc., to gather the essence and allow people to visit and observe, and to arouse their love and desire to purchase. This is the third goal that this association aims to strive for. All the shame of being insulted and ridiculed by the Shanghai women's community will be swept away by this effort, and the vain and extravagant people will see honesty and simplicity, and those who are leisurely and share the profits will see serving the society and saving the waste of family expenses to create the welfare of the people. From hating foreign goods to using domestic goods to participating in improving the manufacturing of domestic goods, our women's community should not shirk its responsibilities in the creation of a new country. From now on, we will determine this new concept, establish a new model for national women, unite as one, be diligent and courageous, and become the advocate for the whole country. This association treads on thin ice and seeks to realize it drop by drop. We hope that all the great men of the community will not hesitate to correct and supervise it. I am very fortunate and sincerely offer this declaration. December 20, 1930.

Citywide Population of Over Three Million in October

Population Statistics Report from the Municipal Public Security Bureau

The Municipal Public Security Bureau has monthly reports on population changes in the city. The September statistics were published in the previous report. It is now known that the bureau's October report shows that the number of households in the city is 186,425, with 176,953 attached households. The number of males is 979,727, and the number of females is 723,847. The number of foreign households is 2,032, with a population of 9,882. The total number of statistical households is 365,410, with a population of 1,713,456. The total population in the special district remains the same as the previous statistics, with 1,393,282 Chinese and 49,393 foreigners, for a total city population of 3,156,131, an increase of 11,326 over September.

Unfortunate Incident Involving Jianghai Merchant Ship

Jianghua Runs Aground

The Jianghua ship of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, which was coming to Shanghai from Hankou carrying a large amount of cargo, ran aground yesterday morning at six o'clock in Zhenjiang. The shipowner, Huang Muzong, believed that the Jianghua was heavily loaded and had a deep draft, so it could not berth at the pontoon. He suggested that the cargo be unloaded using barges, but the Zhenjiang Bureau Chief refused and ordered the ship to berth at the pier, which resulted in the ship running aground. The water there was very shallow. After the ship ran aground, a very dangerous situation arose. The shipowner Huang sent a telegram to the General Bureau, stating that the ship arrived in Zhenjiang at 5:30 this morning. The ship had a very deep draft. I strongly requested to transship the cargo, but the branch bureau ignored it and forced the ship to berth, resulting in the ship running aground. The situation was dire and it was impossible to get out of danger for a while. The bureau did not understand the stakes and insisted on its own way, without any room for negotiation, resulting in this disaster. After the telegram arrived in Shanghai, a second telegram was received at 4 p.m., stating that a small ship was dispatched this morning to tow the Jianghua, and anchors were used, but it was ineffective. The wind and waves blew in, and the tide receded, leaving no way to escape. We will try again when the tide rises. Huang Muzong continued to telegram, saying that the heavily loaded ship ran aground and was very dangerous. Please order the Emei ship, which is sailing upstream from Shanghai today, to Zhenjiang to tow the Jianghua. Also, please send a telegram to the Nanjing Branch Bureau to instruct the ships sailing downstream to detour Zhenjiang to assist in towing and avoid endangering the Jianghua. Yesterday, the Shanghai Bureau had already sent a telegram to the Zhenjiang Branch Bureau, instructing the branch chief to take immediate action to rescue the ship. At the same time, it also telegraphed all the Yangtze River ships sailing downstream to Shanghai to assist in the rescue. It is still unknown whether the ship's hull has been damaged.

Shipping accident

The merchant ship Xiersi of the German-owned North German Lloyd, managed by the American merchant house Meizui Shi Yanghang in this port, carried goods from Germany to Shanghai this time. After unloading the goods in Shanghai, it loaded soybeans and grains and transported them to Beiyang to be transshipped to Europe. On the 18th of this month, it loaded goods from Qingdao and went directly to Kobe. The ship encountered fog and heavy winds just outside the port of Kobe and crashed into a reef. Fortunately, the shipowner telegraphed Japan for help and backed up to escape the danger. Yesterday, a telegram came from Japan saying that a ship had been sent to tow it into Kobe. The ship's hull has been damaged and is currently being repaired at the Kobe shipyard. It will take about ten days to complete the project. The damage to the hull and the loss of goods are being investigated, and it is expected to leave the dock in Japan on the 31st of this month and then sail to Shanghai again.

Discussion on the New Year Holiday Issue

Should Be Handled in Accordance with the National Calendar

After the joint meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees of the City General Chamber of Commerce resolved to handle the current accounts in accordance with the resolutions of the State Council and agreed to set February 15, 1931, as the deadline, some people outside mistakenly thought that the New Year holiday would also be postponed until after February 15. The reporter of Xinsheng News Agency specially visited Wang Xiaolai, chairman of the City General Chamber of Commerce, yesterday to inquire about this issue. According to him, the New Year holiday should of course be handled in accordance with the usual customs of various industries in accordance with the National Calendar. The supplementary measures have also been clearly stipulated by the City Party Department and the City Social Affairs Bureau in the Joint Announcement No. 5096. As for the date of hiring and firing store employees, the General Chamber of Commerce has made a decision due to factual reasons, and is now preparing a document to submit to the government for record. Later, I also met with Wang Yansong, a member of the Standing Committee of the General Chamber of Commerce, who also said that the purpose of his proposal to set a deadline for handling accounts this time was entirely to remedy the commercial difficulties in fact. As for other issues, they should all be handled in accordance with the central government's regulations on promoting the National Calendar and cannot be associated with the deadline for handling accounts.

Wuhu to Open Airmail Route

Starting from the 23rd of This Month

It is heard from the Shanghai Postal Authorities that starting from the 23rd of this month, the China National Aviation Corporation's planes will stop in Wuhu. The airmail rates are the same as those for mailing to Nanjing, Jiujiang, Anqing, and Hankou.

Continued Request to Maintain Original Silver Letter Postage on Chao-Shantou Railway

Telegram from the Overseas Chinese Federation to the Ministry of Railways

The Overseas Chinese Federation received telegrams from the Ministry of Railways and the Shantou Overseas Chinese Silver Letter Bureau Association yesterday regarding the issue of increasing the shipping fees for overseas Chinese silver letters on the Chao-Shantou Railway. It immediately telegraphed the Ministry of Railways, stating: "Respectfully to Minister Sun of the Ministry of Railways in Nanjing, I have received your department's telegram No. 1751, in which you stated that you have learned about the issue of increasing the shipping fees for overseas Chinese silver letters on the Chao-Shantou Railway and have instructed the railway to investigate the details of this case and the previous fee collection methods and report them in detail for verification. Please be informed, etc." Just as we were preparing to reply to the Shantou Overseas Chinese Silver Letter Bureau Association, we received a telegram from the association stating that on the 11th of this month, the Chao-Shantou Railway Company sent a letter stating that the shipping fee for gold and silver currency worth 1,000 yuan would be one yuan, and that items worth less than 1,000 yuan would also be charged according to 1,000 yuan, and that this would be implemented on the 12th of this month. The association believes that the fixed shipping fee is almost doubled compared to the old one, and the deadline is very urgent. Therefore, it sent representatives to negotiate to follow the old method to show preferential treatment to overseas Chinese, and the remittance is carried by the remittance people themselves, which is obviously different from the distribution and cannot be limited to the same. However, the company's attitude is firm and it wants to implement it immediately. The association believes that the increase in fees is too large and harms the lives of overseas Chinese, so it has stopped sending remittances and sent telegrams to overseas Chinese organizations in various ports to appeal for the maintenance of the original method. It has also telegraphed the general association on the day of the letter, requesting that it be the hub of overseas Chinese to protect the interests of overseas Chinese. The President's love for overseas Chinese is to order the Chao-Shantou Railway to collect the remittance shipping fee for overseas Chinese remittances carried by themselves according to the original amount, so as to reduce the burden on overseas Chinese. The President's kindness to the overseas Chinese will be in line with our President. I am at your service."

Business Meeting of the Two Railways Postponed

At the Request of Representatives from Various Chambers of Commerce in Other Ports

Postponed to January 15 of Next Year

It was previously reported that the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration had selected January 5 of 1931 to convene a business meeting in order to develop its business. It is now known that the two railways recently received letters from representatives of various chambers of commerce in other ports, stating that all merchants are following the orders of the National Government to settle accounts and celebrate the New Year in accordance with the National Calendar. If they come to Shanghai immediately after the New Year to attend the meeting, there will be many inconveniences in fact, and they have requested a postponement. The railway authorities believe that this situation is indeed the case, so they have followed the request of the representatives and postponed the meeting date to January 15 of next year.

Follow-up Reports on the典質 (Pawn Shop) Strike

Arrested Workers: One Released, Three Sentenced

Two More Arrested Yesterday, Released Shortly After

Management Held a Meeting Yesterday to Discuss Revising Terms

Yesterday was the third day of the pawn shop workers' strike. All pawn shops in the city remained closed. The four workers arrested the day before were sentenced by the Special District Court yesterday. Three were sentenced to three weeks of detention, while one was immediately released due to wrongful arrest. The strike committee sent a letter to He Kang Pawn Shop, demanding responsibility. Two more workers were arrested yesterday but released shortly after. Management held a meeting yesterday to discuss revising the terms of worker treatment in order to attend the Party Headquarters today for mediation. The situation of both labor and management yesterday is recorded below:

Labor News

Investigation of Arrests: Before 8:00 AM yesterday, investigation teams from various districts set out to investigate whether pawn shops were on strike. Around 9:00 AM, Zhu Haicheng and Fan Rongfa were dispatched by the Central District Special Team Leader to Yikang Pawn Shop on Tiemalu Road to persuade them, when a "bao tan" (detective) arrived and took them to Hongkou Police Station for temporary detention. After the inspector inquired and found that they had not disturbed public order, they were released. All other pawn shops in various districts remained on strike throughout the day and did not open.

Court Ruling: At 3:40 PM the day before yesterday,

Workers Cheng Guangzu, Shao Chunsheng, Wang Junyan, and Zhou Hanyun were arrested by the Harbin Road Police Station while persuading He Kang Pawn Shop on Dongjiaxing Road to close. They were detained. Yesterday morning at 9:00 AM, they were transferred to the Sixth Tribunal of the Special District Court for questioning. Huang Shenkang, manager of He Kang Pawn Shop, appeared in court as the plaintiff. Li Fulin and Zhu Tianqi were dispatched as worker representatives to attend the hearing. As a result of the trial, Cheng Guangzu, Shao Chunsheng, and Wang Junyan were deemed to have disrupted order by entering He Kang Pawn Shop and forcing a strike, and each was sentenced to three weeks of detention. Zhou Hanyun was immediately released because he did not enter He Kang Pawn Shop and was merely observing. Cheng Guangzu, Shao Chunsheng, and Wang Junyan declared in court that they refused to accept the verdict and filed an appeal. The workers' union also hired a lawyer yesterday to appeal to the Second Branch of the High Court at any time.

Petition to Protect the Pawn Shop Workers' Union: Because the strike has been orderly this time, but investigators have been arrested by the police, the union feels endangered and has petitioned the Municipal Party Headquarters and the People's Training Committee to provide protection for the workers and sent representatives Wang Ganchen and Deng Dunli to the Municipal Party Headquarters with the petition. At the same time, they petitioned the Social Affairs Bureau to request that the Special District Court issue a notice to all police stations not to arbitrarily interfere with orderly strike movements.

General Assembly Resolution: More than 300 striking workers held a general membership meeting at the union at 4:00 PM yesterday. Chairman Wang Ganchen reported on the strike situation throughout the city from various district investigation teams. They then discussed: (1) Receiving the instruction from the Municipal Party Headquarters and the People's Training Committee to convene both parties for mediation at 1:00 PM on the 21st (today) and designating four responsible representatives to attend the case; it was resolved to appoint Wang Ganchen, Cheng Tianfen, Jin Futian, and Cheng Zijun as representatives, and Hu Jinzhang and Li Fulin as observers. (2) The condition in Article 2 regarding a pay increase, the minimum limit that can be agreed upon for signing, should be discussed; it was resolved that the case should be handled by the signing representatives. (3) The entire set of conditions should be handled by the signing representatives with full authority without discussion; the resolution was passed. (4) It was proposed that all members of the union must gather at the union tomorrow without fail; the resolution was passed. (5) Due to the cold weather, winter clothes should be sent to the arrested comrades in the police station; it was resolved to hand the clothes to the manager of He Kang to send.

Condolences and Aid: Yesterday, representatives from the Soy Sauce Workers' Union, Weng Ruifu; the Postal Workers' Union, Liu Xinquan; the Pharmaceutical Workers' Union, Fang Qingjian; the British American Tobacco Factory Workers' Union, Wang Ajin; the China Merchants Bureau No. 5 Wharf Workers' Union, Yu Xianting; the Sanitation Workers' Union, Jiang Qimin; the Ship Timber Workers' Union, Ye Xiangnie; the Rice and Grain Workers' Union, Sun ZhengGuo; the Silk and Cloth Dyeing Workers' Union, Zhu XiaoYun; all went to the pawn shop workers' union to offer condolences. All workers' unions in the city and each union issued a declaration of aid.

Management News

Report to the Authorities: The Pawn Shop Trade Association previously received instructions from the Municipal Party Headquarters, the People's Training Committee, and the Social Affairs Bureau to dispatch responsible representatives to the Party Headquarters on the 21st (today) to await mediation. Yesterday, a document was submitted to the People's Training Committee and the Social Affairs Bureau, stating that the association's members are divided into old and new, and due to different circumstances, the treatment of workers has not been consistent. For example, the agreement signed by labor and management on December 30, 1927, should be mutually observed, but when management earnestly implemented it, it was often rejected by workers, who often favored old practices. Therefore, various members of the association believe that the workers' union's request this time is still not thorough. Before the slowdown occurred, it was difficult for management to prepare in advance, and since responsible representatives had not been designated, they did not dare to rashly come forward and respond. Now, due to the previous instructions, a temporary emergency meeting of members was convened on the afternoon of the 18th. However, due to the suddenness of the event, only about 30 firms attended, and they all felt that the response to the workers' request could not be decided by a small number of firms. They had to reschedule a general assembly of all members on the afternoon of the 20th to jointly deliberate and then designate responsible representatives to follow the instructions of the Municipal Party Headquarters and the People's Training Committee to go there on the afternoon of the 21st with the Social Affairs Bureau to await mediation without delay. However, considering that the purpose of the pawn industry is to serve the people in addition to business, especially during the winter season, many poor households are waiting to redeem their clothes to keep warm and pawn miscellaneous items for food. If the slowdown continues and the business is suspended, it will not only be detrimental to both labor and management but also affect the livelihoods of the poor and the local security. Moreover, since the labor-management issue has been ordered to be mediated by the Council and the Social Affairs Bureau, we can wait quietly for the solution. The expression is unnecessary to resort to a slowdown. In addition to reporting the actual situation of the association for handling, we implore the Council to quickly issue an order to the workers' union to quickly resume work in order to maintain the livelihoods of the poor and the local security for public convenience. Sincerely submitted by the Pawn Shop Trade Association of Shanghai to the Municipal Party Headquarters of Shanghai and the Social Affairs Bureau of Shanghai.

Yesterday's Meeting: Members of the Trade Association decided to hold a membership meeting at the Lifeng Xiaoji on the half-floor of No. 6 Rongshou Lane, Beihai Road, at 1:00 PM yesterday. At around 3:00 PM, only a few members had arrived and were exchanging pleasantries. Suddenly, a burly northerner wearing a black robe and a black cloth around his head entered the building, claiming that his name was Xu Sanxing, that he had come to Shanghai from Guangdong, and that a few days ago, due to lack of funds, he had pawned his clothes at Yutai Pawn Shop east of the Little World. Now, he was going to Nanjing on business and needed to redeem his clothes to take to Nanjing, but the pawn shop was closed and he could not redeem them, so he had come to inquire. Then, Cheng Rufu, manager of Yutai Pawn Shop, issued a letter instructing him to redeem his clothes, and he retreated. At 4:10 PM, 52 members arrived and announced the opening of the meeting. Yu Shaoqing and Fang Minfu (on behalf of Cheng Rufu) were elected as chairmen to discuss the revised conditions proposed by the Workers' Union in great detail. Yu Langxi also reported on the revised content in order to present opinions when attending the Party Headquarters for mediation this afternoon. (Ri Ri News Agency)

Local News 2

Assassination of Foreign Staff Member in Wusong

Mr. Zhubielin of the Dredging Bureau

Shot Dead by Bandits at 7 PM Last Night

Mr. Zhubielin, a foreign staff member and the head of the northern machine shop of the engineering department of the Wusong Zhanghuabang Dredging Bureau, was shot and killed by bandits yesterday evening at 7 PM after leaving work at 5 PM to take the train to Shanghai. Details are as follows:

Bandit Ambush: Mr. Zhu, accompanied by a Chinese shop worker named Jia, left the engineering department gate at 7 o'clock. Not dozens of steps away, near the back gate of the Hebo Si Yamen, the area was extremely deserted at night, so the bandits lurked by the roadside unnoticed. When Mr. Zhu approached, he was suddenly shot. The bullet hit a vital spot in the temple, and he fell to the ground and died. The shop worker, upon hearing the gunshot and seeing his master fall, was terrified and immediately fled back. The assailant, seeing that his goal had been achieved, fled in the chaos. The gatekeeper, Gong Xiaogou, saw the shop worker flee back and learned of the incident. The two went to report to Mr. Klaomo, the head of the southern construction department.

Death in the Street: Upon hearing the news, Mr. Ke went to the scene and saw Mr. Zhu's body wearing a white-gray coat, white woolen gloves, and black leather shoes. His clothes were neat, and he lay dead in the middle of the road with his head facing south and his feet facing north. Inspection revealed that the bullet entered the right temple and exited the left temple, with blood flowing all over the ground. The sight was unbearable. Mr. Ke checked his pockets and found a 5-yuan note from the Bank of China, 25 copper coins, a string of keys, and an empty envelope. There was nothing else. He then went to Shanghai to report to the General Bureau.

Background: Mr. Zhu was originally Russian but later became a French citizen. He was about 30 years old and unmarried. He was proficient in Chinese language and writing and could directly communicate with workers. He was dispatched from the Shanghai Bureau to the machine shop on July 1 of this year and had only been there for five months when he was suddenly killed. The reason is unknown.

Police Investigation: The chief of the first police station of the seventh district and members of the security corps rushed to investigate the scene and apprehend the perpetrator, but they were gone. The police chief rushed to report to Director Zhang Jiguang in Songhu. Director Zhang, along with detectives Yu Peifa and patrol officers, went to the scene to investigate the situation. They are currently searching for the culprit.

Assassination of Wang Baozhan, Standing Committee Member of the Rickshaw Guild

Shot by Assailants in the Lane

Critically Injured and Died

Family Speculates on the Reason for the Attack

Related to Rickshaw License Fees

Wang Baozhan, a native of Funing and a standing committee member of the Shanghai Rickshaw Trade Association, was shot by assailants in a lane while returning home from a bathhouse around 6:00 PM last night. The assailant escaped without a trace. He was rushed to the hospital by his family but died due to the severity of his injuries. There are several theories as to the reason for the killing, but the dispute over rickshaw license fees seems the most likely.

Returning Home After Bathing: Wang Baozhan, styled Qinzhai, was 55 years old, a native of Funing, and worked as a rickshaw puller. Before the Shanghai Rickshaw Trade Association was established, he served as the chairman of the Northern Shanghai Rickshaw Guild. After the merger of the north and south guilds last year, he was elected as a standing committee member of the Shanghai Rickshaw Trade Association. He lived at No. 1 Dexiang Lane, Hengfeng Road, Zhabei, not far from the guild's office on Datong Road, so he often walked back and forth. Around 6:00 PM last night, while returning home from the Huayang Chi Bathhouse at the intersection of 　Zhong　 Road, he was suddenly shot by an assailant lurking by the roadside at the entrance of Dexiang Lane. The assassin shot him from behind. Wang Baozhan turned to flee upon hearing the gunshot, but the assailant fired several more shots at his face, all hitting vital spots. At this time, Wang's family in the house heard the gunshots and were alarmed. They then heard someone knocking urgently on the door. Upon opening it, Wang Baozhan had 　staggered　 into the parlor, pointing to his chest with his left hand, which was covered in blood. He called out that he had been shot and pointed to his abdomen to indicate. When asked by his family who had shot him, Wang was incomprehensible.

Death from Injuries: Wang's family reported the incident to the second police station of the fourth district and requested the arrest of the assailant. They also rushed Wang Baozhan to Baolong Hospital on Baker Road for treatment. However, he died halfway due to the severity of his injuries. After arriving at the hospital, the doctor examined him and found three gunshot wounds: one on the left wrist, one below the navel, and another on the lower abdomen. The bullets had all passed through. According to eyewitnesses, the assailant was wearing a dark coat that was longer than his knees and a felt hat. He was about 23 or 24 years old. Before the attack, someone had handed Wang several copies of the resolution passed by the executive committee of the Rickshaw Guild outside the lane, wrapped in newspaper. When Wang was shot, he was still holding the newspaper in his hand, so the paper was stained with blood. However, the person who handed the package said that he did not see anyone lurking around when approaching the lane.

Reason for the Killing: According to Wang Baozhan's family, the killing was definitely the work of an enemy. As for why there was such a dire consequence, the dispute over rickshaw license fees seems the most likely reason. The deceased, Wang Baozhan, was outspoken and resourceful in the guild and was often elected as the guild's representative to negotiate with the Chinese and foreign rickshaw guilds in the concessions. Recently, the municipal government has ordered the Chinese and foreign rickshaw guilds in the concessions to join the Municipal Rickshaw Trade Association before April 1 of next year to ensure uniformity, otherwise the Chinese territory license will not be issued. It is said that Wang Baozhan had worked hard on this matter, which caused him to be resented by a few people, resulting in his death. Wang's son, named Xian Gu, is a lawyer and has reported the incident to the Public Security Bureau requesting the arrest of the assailant.

Tongwen College

School Servant Hanged Himself with Grievance

Served for Twenty-Eight Years

Highly Trusted by School Staff and Students

Took the Blame for Nephew's Loss of Huge Sum of Money

Unable to Find a Solution, Hanged Himself with Grievance

Li Hailin, a 42-year-old school servant from Hanyang, Hubei, at the Dongwen College on Hongqiao Road, was found hanged to death in the school yesterday morning. The Chinese students of the school suspect that Li committed suicide out of anger and resentment and have organized a support group to redress his grievances and find ways to help his family.

Taking the Blame for Nephew: Li Hailin has been serving as a school servant at Dongwen College for twenty-eight years. He is usually diligent and simple, and is trusted by the school authorities and students. He handles the delivery of letters, remittances, and purchases of miscellaneous items. Li has a nephew named Zhu Minggao, who is 21 years old. Li introduced him to the school to work as a servant. Whenever Li had to go out, Zhu would assist him in everything. One afternoon, at around 1:00 PM, Li Hailin drove a motorized bicycle to the post office and banks on North Sichuan Road to remit money. He received more than 1,350 yuan in banknotes, which he placed in the bicycle seat and entrusted to Zhu to guard. When he returned to school, the car passed by Tibet Road. Li got out of the car to buy a clothing box and instructed Zhu Minggao to pay attention to guarding the money. Who knew that Zhu was already gone when the business was finished and the money was completely lost. Li was shocked and hurried to look for him in various places, but found nothing. So he immediately returned to the school to inform the accountant, Kobayashi, who reported it to the police and the Japanese consulate to investigate Zhu's whereabouts. However, the school authorities blamed Li for the mistake, ordered him to find Zhu, and promised to find a way to raise money to compensate.

Sudden Suicide: After taking the blame for his nephew, Li's spirit was extremely distracted, and the school authorities suspected Li of conspiring in the matter and ordered a Japanese detective to interrogate Li. He was summoned to the accounting office the night before and interrogated in many ways. However, Li was not involved in the matter, so of course there was no way. The Japanese detective told him that he had to be taken to the police station tomorrow morning (yesterday morning) and handed over to his nephew. Li's fear increased. Yesterday morning, the school servants suddenly did not see Li Hailin. At first, they thought he had gone home, but his wife also said that he had not returned. They searched everywhere, but found nothing. It was not until around 11:00 AM that a son of a school worker discovered that Li had hanged himself in the car room. He had already died. The school reported to the police. However, Hongqiao Road is a cross-border construction. The sixth district and the second division of the Public Security Bureau sent the police to investigate the matter and ordered the school not to move the body to maintain police power.

A Family of Ten: Li Hailin married Zhu and has eight children. A family of ten all depend on Li alone. The eldest son, Peiyong, is 16 years old and is working and studying at Dongwen College. The second son, Peiyuan, is 13 years old and is studying at Hongqiao Road Primary School. The third son is ten years old, the fourth son is nine years old, the fifth and sixth are daughters, one is six years old and the other is four years old. The seventh son is three years old and the eighth son was born the day before yesterday. The Chinese students of the school Li Meng are very pitiful and his family is screaming in grief. Therefore, a support association has been organized to redress the grievances of the matter and to provide relief to his widow and orphans to comfort the dead.

National New Year

Still Prohibited from Setting Off Firecrackers

The Municipal Public Security Bureau Issues Orders to Subordinates to Comply

Setting off firecrackers is most likely to cause a fire and can easily cause misunderstandings. In order to maintain public order, the Municipal Public Security Bureau has repeatedly issued orders and notices to prohibit them. Now that the National New Year is approaching, the Public Security Bureau and the Social Affairs Bureau are particularly concerned that people may set off firecrackers to celebrate the New Year, which will only waste money and be of no benefit to citizens. The Public Security Bureau has issued an order to its subordinates to continue to strictly prohibit them.

Three Bandits Executed by Firing Squad

Jiang Haoyuan, Chang Miaquan, Chou Jinpu

Zhou Rangsan, a staff member of Meifu Foreign Company and a native of Yong, was kidnapped on the morning of August 27 at No. 1360 Hed Road, Shanghai West, when he left his house to go to work. He was rescued by the Jingansi Police Station, and one bandit, A Da, was killed on the spot. Five were captured and handed over to the Special District Local Court. Jiang Haoyuan, Yang Miaquan, and Chou Jinpu were all sentenced to death. Wang Aqing was sentenced to six years in prison. Zhang Xingbao was declared innocent after being questioned. The case was reported to the superiors for review. It is now approved that the three men of Jiang, Yang and Chou will be executed according to law to show sternness. The police station was notified to take the three criminals from the West Prison to the Special Court yesterday morning. Judge Cheng Shangfeng opened the court and declared that today was the day of execution and asked if there were any last words. Jiang confessed that he was 28 years old and from Tongzhou. He had already written a letter in prison this morning and asked the police detective Liu to hand it over to his relatives. He said that his death was not a pity and that he would avenge himself after death. When he was arrested, he had two double cents and 19 copper coins hidden in his body, which were stored in the police station. He requested that the money be used to buy long ingots to burn at the execution ground. There were also two pawn tickets, which he asked to be attached to the letter. Yang Miaquan confessed that he was 21 years old from Tongzhou and asked to inform his maternal uncle Chen Arong at the Huatong Electric Bulb Factory on Yulin Road and ask him to tell his father not to be sad, knowing that life and death are predetermined. He also instructed him to go to collect his body quickly. Chou was also from Tongzhou and only 26 years old. He confessed that he was harmed by Chen Heqing and requested to send a letter to Mao Daodao, a friend of his, at the Rixin Silk Factory, Panshijiaba South Bridge East, to tell his father-in-law, Chou Hongsheng, that he was a son-in-law and that although he had two children, his wife was still young and asked his father-in-law to recruit another son-in-law. After Judge Cheng questioned them, he ordered the detectives to escort the three criminals to the Caohejing Jiangsu Second Prison execution ground by car. Lei Renlong, a prosecutor appointed by the Shanghai Local Court Procuratorate, was the supervising officer and ordered Police Chief Yang Deshan and Police Officer Chen Xihui to lead many execution police officers, including Gu Hanqing, Xue Bingzhang, and Xu Guoguang, to the execution ground. After the judge took the seat and questioned each criminal, the judge ordered the execution. Police Chief Yang commanded the execution police to take them down and execute them by firing squad. The bodies were collected by the court to wait for their families to claim them.

Meeting on Dredging the Shentan

Construction to Begin After Approval from the Ministry

The Dredging Bureau has received letters from British and British Chambers of Commerce and Chinese and foreign shipping companies stating that after dredging the Shentan outside Wusongkou, several meetings have been held and opinions have been solicited from Chinese and foreign shipping circles on fundraising. Customs Commissioner Mei proposed to increase the dredging tax by seven li on imported foreign goods. If this is not enough, the bureau will allocate from special funds. The bureau recently convened a bureau affairs meeting. Director Song Ziliang, Customs Commissioner Mei, and Secretary Guo of the Hebo Division attended. Chief Engineer Chaderi reported on the planning, design, construction equipment, expenses, and time limit for dredging the Shentan. After discussion between Director Song and Customs Commissioner Mei, they agreed that dredging the Shentan was a major task for developing Shanghai's commerce and should be carried out actively. As a result, a memorial was drafted and submitted to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for approval before proceeding.

French Tram Corrects Wording

Supervised by the Public Utilities Bureau

Changed to French Commercial Tram

French commercial trams operating in the city temporarily cannot be stopped due to established cases. The Third, Fifth, and Sixth routes are the only ones with the words (French Concession Tram) marked on the outside of the carriages. The First District Party Department of this city believed that this would cause a bad impression on the citizens and submitted it to the Municipal Executive Committee, which sent a letter to the Municipal Government instructing them to change it to (French Commercial Tram) to avoid confusion. The Municipal Public Utilities Bureau sent two letters to the French Electric Light and Tram Company urging them to make the correction, which has now been made uniformly. The bureau has also sent a letter to the Public Security Bureau and the district offices instructing the chief police officers to pay special attention to preventing any uncorrected trams from entering the city in order to emphasize the importance of the law.

New Sassoon Purchases Taixing Bank Site

Taixing Bank Continues to Operate as Usual

The Shanghai Times reported that the Taixing Bank property on Nanjing Road has been sold to the New Sassoon Bank. The transaction was completed yesterday (the 19th) at the British Consulate General, and Sassoon contracted to lease the property to Taixing for business. According to the owner of Taixing, the bank will continue to operate as usual. The property covers slightly less than three mu and sold for 900,000 taels.

Second Day of the China Society Photographic Exhibition

Yesterday was the second day of the Fourth Photographic Exhibition of the China Society. From morning to evening, it drizzled lightly, but visitors continued to come in an endless stream. Many photography technicians and photography enthusiasts inquired about the methods of making oil-based and gelatin-based photographs, which were explained in detail by members of the society. In the afternoon, Lang Jingshan introduced Gaston, a famous American photographer, to visit the exhibition. Gaston praised the exhibits of the China Society and was particularly impressed with Shao Woyun, Lang Jingshan, Zhu Shuren, and Hu Boxiang. After viewing the exhibition, Gaston immediately returned to his residence and sent nine of his masterpieces to be displayed at the exhibition.

Highlights of Today's Theater Performances

Tea Room Worker at Jinan University Drowns Himself

Due to Economic Pressure

Yesterday morning at 11:00 AM, a young man suddenly jumped into the river at the Jinliyuan Wharf of the China Merchants Bureau. Fortunately, he was spotted by Chinese constable No. 66 of the water police station, who rescued him from the water and took him back to the police station for questioning. He claimed his name was Liu Shixuan, 23 years old, from Anhui Province. He used to be a tea room worker at Jinan University in Zhenru and is now unemployed. He is suffering from severe economic pressure and sought death. The police chief instructed the detective to go to the school to inquire and confirmed the facts. Cui Zhonggao, a tea worker at the school's School of Business, went to the police station and brought Liu back to find ways to help him.

Appeals from Street Vendors on Minquan Road in the French Concession

Street Vendor Association Asks General Supervisor Fei to Maintain

On Minquan Road in the French Concession, from Xiaobeimen to Dongxinqiao Street, there are various street vendors setting up stalls for business. Because there are illegal vendors setting up gambling stalls, gathering pedestrians, and obstructing traffic, the Four Ming Guild sent a letter to the French Concession Police to ban them. The police, after receiving the request, evicted all the vendors in the area, regardless of whether they were legitimate or not, and sent a patrolman to guard and ban all legitimate vendors from setting up stalls. As a result, about 70 vendors immediately lost their jobs. The French Concession Street Vendor Association has sent a letter to the Four Ming Guild to maintain the livelihoods of the street vendors. The guild has also sent a letter to the French Concession Police requesting that legitimate vendors be treated leniently and that the guild's directors, 　Qiaqing Jun, responded to the association stating that the guild would not interfere with legitimate vendors setting up stalls in front of the guild. The association has repeatedly requested the French Concession Police, but they still refuse to allow them to set up stalls. Therefore, the livelihoods of the vendors are very difficult to maintain. Yesterday, the association sent a letter to General Supervisor Fei asking him to maintain their livelihoods.

Zhaojun, formerly a prostitute in the Qunyufang brothel on Shantou Road, was earlier redeemed and taken as a concubine by Yang Dinghou. Page 16

-zhou and is twenty-two years old. Formerly, the two defendants forced her into a brothel in the year 16 of the Republic (1927). After being taken as a concubine by Yang Dinghou, their relationship was harmonious. This year, in February, the defendant, Song Shi, came and said she would take her to Suzhou for sightseeing, and she went with her. A Favorite Concubine Abuses the Wife, Who Attempts Suicide by Drowning

Ye Jincheng is Devoid of Compassion

Ye Jincheng, 42 years old, from Anhui Province, resides at the east end of the railway north of Fanwangdubang in western Shanghai. He works as a foreman in a factory and has accumulated some savings, making him somewhat well-off. His wife, Wu Shi, is the same age. However, Wu Shi has not yet had any children, and her lap remains empty. Because Ye was eager to have a son, he took Zhang A'da, a woman from Yangzhou, as a concubine this spring, introduced by a friend. After she entered the house, they lived together. The relationship between the wife and concubine was like fire and water, but the wife, Wu Shi, was naturally weak and had to endure in silence. The concubine, however, was only twenty-four years old, of fair appearance, and of fierce temperament, so Ye doted on her greatly and oppressed his original wife severely. Recently, Wu Shi, unable to bear it any longer, quarreled with the concubine constantly. Around 8 p.m. the day before yesterday, Ye was having dinner with the concubine when, for some reason, a fierce argument suddenly broke out again. Relying on her husband's power, the concubine immediately stepped forward and beat Wu Shi. Unexpectedly, her husband not only did not stop her but helped the concubine beat Wu Shi severely. Overwhelmed with grief and indignation, Wu Shi secretly slipped out the back door and jumped into a small creek to commit suicide. Fortunately, a neighbor saw her, braved the rain, and rushed to rescue her. She was drenched and had swallowed a lot of water. She was resuscitated and fortunately survived.

Continued Report on the Strike of Employees in Liquor Stores

The Situation is More Tense Than Before

There is Fear of a Full-Scale Strike

(3) Responsibilities during the strike period are to be assigned to designated personnel, including propaganda, transportation, secret investigation, investigation, and clerical duties. It was resolved to divide it into four groups of ten people each, with one person as the leader. Cen Laifu, Zhou Rudao, Wang Hede, and Han A'ming were appointed. (2) The organization of a picket team. It was resolved to hand it over to the Executive Committee for handling. A request to investigate Zhu Houfu, an assistant at the levy office, was approved. (3) How to proceed if negotiations fail. It was resolved to proceed in accordance with the Executive Committee's resolutions.

Time for Government Employees to Undergo Opium Addiction Checks

The Municipal Government Issues Instructions for All Agencies to Comply With

The municipal government yesterday issued instructions to the bureaus and investigation committees, saying: For the purpose of knowing the facts of the case, the approval of the Tobacco Prohibition Committee's consultation is hereby announced. The rules for the opium addiction checks of government employees have already been announced, but there are no clear provisions regarding the time limit in the rules. Repeated inquiries have been received from various provincial governments that if opium addicts are reported or accused and receive a notice to undergo a check, they deliberately delay the time for rehabilitation, which can easily obscure the facts and lose the original intention of legal punishment. Therefore, based on the above meaning, a proposal was prepared and submitted to the 60th and 64th committee meetings for discussion and resolution. It was resolved that the regulations for the implementation of tobacco prohibition stipulate that local authorities may establish addiction check centers, then civil servants in all provinces should undergo addiction checks nearby, and a notice should be sent to the governments of all provinces, instructing them to inform all those who are checked that those who fail to comply within three days of receiving the notice will be deemed to be addicts. When it is necessary to check officers of the army, navy, and air force agencies and civil servants of overseas embassies, the relevant chiefs may be responsible for designating doctors nearby in accordance with the aforementioned time limit. In addition to the separate consultation, a corresponding consultation is requested for verification and notification of compliance, etc. In addition to separate orders, this order is hereby issued, instructing the bureau to be informed for compliance with this order.

No Need to Detain Ships in Collisions

The Responsibility is Borne by the Company

The Shanghai County Government received instructions from the Civil Affairs Department yesterday, saying: For the matter of notification, it is announced that the provincial government's instructions are approved. According to the Zhenjiang Shipping Association's report, the Zhenjiang Shipping Workers' Union stated that all members of the union reported that in the Huai River, whenever a passenger accidentally falls into the water and dies, the water authorities would detain the crew members regardless of the reason and subject them to all kinds of illegal treatment, requesting maintenance, etc. After deliberation, it was decided to send a letter to the Shipping Association to jointly plan a guarantee method, etc. During the performance of their duties, all the actions of the crew members are the actions of the company as a legal entity, not the actions of the individuals themselves. Even in the event of a collision, before the right and wrong are determined according to the navigation rules, the county governments arbitrarily detain the ships and retain the crew members pointed out as defendants to show intimidation, which hinders the peace and order of the passengers, and the company suffers great losses, which is not based on the law, nor is it fair in principle. Moreover, the company is a private legal entity and there is no risk of escape. The suspected crime is only due to negligence or dereliction of duty by the crew members, which is very different from intentional crimes. There is no need to detain the ships and crew members. It is often seen that in large cities, when a car accident occurs, the police only record the car number and allow it to drive away before taking appropriate legal action. Why can't the same be done for ship collisions, recording the company and ship name and allowing them to temporarily transport other passengers? Cars and ships are both transportation businesses, but the treatment by government agencies is different. The Department of Transportation requested the Department of Transportation to inform all local authorities that in the future, except for major cases in which the current offender poses a risk of escape and is difficult to capture without immediate arrest, in the event of a collision, if the company can be held responsible, please do not arbitrarily detain them in order to protect the law and protect human rights, etc. In accordance with the notification, the County Government and the Water and Land Public Security Bureau have been instructed to comply with the procedures in this order, the County Chief has been instructed to comply with the above.

The Robustness of French Safes

Water, Fire, and Thieves Can Be Permanently Avoided

The Dewar & Company on the second floor of the HSBC Building on the Bund in this city is now the manager of the French Fesey Factory's novel safe. Its structure is different from ordinary safes. The lock is locked with a secret mechanism. Even if a novice has the key, it cannot be opened. Its surroundings have multiple layers of specially tempered steel plates that are as sharp as electric drills. The interlayer is made of specially made moisture-proof and fire-resistant materials. Even if the safe is immersed in water and fire for many years, the banknotes and documents inside can be preserved. Therefore, this kind of safe can absolutely guarantee against the dangers of water, fire, and thieves.

Free Talk

Remembering Mr. Sun Jingseng Chunmeng

Mr. Sun Jingseng of Wujiang was my respected teacher. He taught at Minli Middle School for more than twenty years.

Mr. Sun was knowledgeable and had a strong memory. His personality was especially gentle and approachable. All alumni of Minli respected and admired Mr. Sun. As a teacher, he was authoritative but not harsh. His teaching, even in the smallest word or action, could transform people through virtue. I remember one hot summer evening after class, some students moved their seats to the playground to enjoy the cool air. The moon was bright, and the young students, being playful, stacked chairs and benches to make a jumping game. After the group dispersed, they left the benches and chairs in disarray. Mr. Sun, upon seeing this, did not

scold them but personally moved everything back to its original place. Later, those who had been jumping heard of this and felt deeply ashamed, saying to each other, "We were undisciplined and caused Mr. Sun so much trouble." After this, on days when Mr. Sun was on duty, they would diligently restrain themselves. Mr. Sun, though approaching old age, was diligent in his studies and never tired, always fearing to lag behind. His work and rest were always scheduled. Every morning he would rise and practice calligraphy in large characters. During breaks, he would browse private collections. In the evening, he would study elementary texts carefully, researching and investigating until midnight before stopping. When I lived at the school, my room was close to Mr. Sun's. Every dawn when I woke up, I would hear the sound of grinding ink and occasional coughing from the neighboring room, indicating that Mr. Sun had already risen and was practicing calligraphy. This was his routine year after year. In the year Yichou, when Mr. Sun turned sixty, he instructed his sons in advance not to follow worldly customs and hold a celebratory banquet. On his birthday, he drafted several self-congratulatory poems and changed his name to "Wuwun." Some said that Mr. Sun was being self-deprecating. I believe that the phrase "at forty or fifty, one is unheard of" in the Analects is merely Confucius encouraging future generations. Could someone as broad-minded as Mr. Sun truly care about being heard of or not? In the past, when the Zhou dynasty declined, gentlemen sang about the rabbit and the monkey, wanting to avoid being awakened. Mr. Sun, witnessing the changes of the times, was likely also moved by this. I have been away from Mr. Sun for five years. I often think of my teacher and feel deeply nostalgic. Recently, I read Mr. Sun's memorial inscription for Mr. Su and could vividly picture Mr. Sun with his graying beard and hair, pacing back and forth under the long corridor in the school, holding a scroll and reciting with feeling. Mr. Sun was skilled in poetry and classical prose. His poetic style was close to that of Bai Juyi. His prose followed the Tongcheng school, being smooth and subtle, capturing its tranquil and distant essence.

Mei Lian Guo

Mei Lanfang's stage appearances in Shanghai were met with many gifts of couplets. Phrases like "Orchid fragrance permeates nine acres, news spreads beyond China," and "Doctor of foreign literature, king of the Chinese acting world," were clever and beautiful. However, one couplet, with only eight characters, was subtly meaningful, classic, and precise. Mei Lanfang passed it on, indicating its special merit. What were those eight characters? "Zhendan Wenxue (Alas, My King)." The giver was the horn player Tao Jia Yao, and the author was the writer Tao Zaidong.

From Zheng Yimei

During the day, there is the warmth to enjoy, no less than wearing a sable coat. At night, there is wine to pour, better than leaning on beauties.

Barbers possess skill above the neck, but are not valued by society.

Shanghai trams have first class and third class, but no second class, highlighting the prominence of the first class.

Stage scenery in movies often only has one side that can be viewed straight on, not from the side. In reality, many things in society are like this and cannot be seen through.

A single folding screen hides much romantic longing.

A lamp, a quilt, a soup, a jar, and a book – this is my only solace on cold nights.

Eating too much candy can damage teeth, so rather than sharing sweetness with others, I prefer to endure bitterness myself.

Someone who enjoys reading the small articles attached to newspapers is definitely not boorish.

To befriend the ancients and associate with contemporary talents – only then can one be worthy of the title "socialite."

The blush on a beauty's face is the only color in the realm of love.

Observe the world with a cool head and read books with an open mind.

Speaking about one's profession at every turn is a major taboo for someone away from home.

Do not walk the path of extremes; leave room for future connections.

By looking at the furnishings, calligraphy, and paintings in someone's house, one can know whether they are refined or vulgar.

In the past, having money made one bold; now, having money makes one timid.

If you absentmindedly mail a letter without sticking a stamp, the anxiety is indescribable.

It's easy to seek the form, but difficult to seek the spirit. Therefore, China's Westernization is merely about form, not spirit.

To read books without seeking deep understanding is something said by exceptionally intelligent people. If we are of average ability, we should chew on every word. Using writing to sell fame is most often empty.

The British Anti-Rat Week by Qiushui

Everyone knows the harm rats cause. Spreading plague and contaminating food are not limited to gnawing on clothes and destroying objects. Hygienists consider rats to be humanity's greatest enemy and try various methods to exterminate them. However, rats reproduce extremely quickly. Their extermination is endless. The British government has an annual Anti-Rat Week, during which the entire nation rises up and fiercely battles rats, hoping to raise public awareness and eradicate rats from human society as soon as possible. This method is excellent.

Equal Strength. The annual Anti-Rat Week began on November 10th this year. At that time, pharmacies and private clinics across the country did their best to display various rat poisons and rat-catching tools for public viewing. Enthusiastic people in various places even gathered comrades to declare war on rats or organized lecture teams to go to remote rural areas to promote rat resistance. Rat-catching experts from various places printed booklets with various rat-catching methods and distributed them to various places for selection. For a time, the whole country was stirred up, and the rats shivered in fear, feeling as if they could not live another day. However, rats are cunning and can foresee disasters. Although the attacks inflicted on them by humans are fierce, their offspring continue to multiply endlessly. According to experts, there are 40 million people in the UK and Wales, and the number of rats in the UK is about the same. With forces so evenly matched, it is difficult to determine the outcome of the battle.

Specially Killing Females. There are about two ways to resist rats: live capture and poisoning. Live capture mostly uses cages, traps, and sweet bait to lure them in and then kill them. Poisoning mostly uses various poisons mixed into cakes and bait so that they swallow them in one bite, and the poison takes effect in their stomachs, making it impossible to save them. Recently, there have even been those who use (poisonous gas) to attack rats. Once used in a room, rats can be wiped out in one fell swoop. However, poisoning can kill people. People cannot get close after application. This is a problem. Rat-catching experts in the UK say that if you want to exterminate rats, you must use the (Rodin) method. What is the Rodin method? It is the latest rat-catching method. The inventor's name is Rodin, hence the name. Those who use this method only kill female rats and not males. Since the battle line is narrower, success is easier. Females are the source of reproduction. Once the females are killed, the males will naturally be difficult to survive for long. It's a good method. There is one more thing to add: rats are good at traveling. To find food or escape, they can travel up to 150 miles. Therefore, the method of catching rats is to have simultaneous operations in various places, with nets densely spread and no gaps to escape. The extermination of rats is almost certain.

Travelogue of Southeast Asia (106)

Burmese monks are very knowledgeable and often say to me: "Our Burma will inevitably suffer the catastrophe of communism in the future." I asked him the reason. He replied: "China and India both have communist parties, and the killing machine is spreading. Burma is located between China and India and will inevitably be affected sooner or later." However, we do not think so. We believe that Siam and Burma are both Buddhist countries. Although they will suffer the catastrophe of communism, their people are kind and will suffer less.

The roads in Mandalay are flat, straight and wide, quite like Beijing. The houses are fresh and new, like Nanjing. However, the land is dry and dusty. There is a good method in Burmese cities that can be learned. Street layouts often use numbers. Mandalay's street names, both vertical and horizontal, are mostly numbers from one to one hundred. The Chinese streets in Rangoon are also like this, but streets that are not Chinese do not use this name. I think using numbers to name streets is a very good method. In ancient China, the method of craftsmen governing the country in the Rites of Zhou first involved dividing longitude and latitude. Those that can be examined now, such as the city of Qufu, although small, have clear longitude and latitude in the north, south, east and west. The new Shandong concession also uses longitude and latitude to name its streets, which is very convenient for searching. Now the street names in various cities are messy and directionless. How can they compare to our ancient system?

On the 15th, introduced by Xie Dunming, I visited Burmese person RYAWHLAO. He is also the secretary of the Mandalay Evangelical Association. He read my English letter and liked it very much. I also visited Burmese person Ge Ba. The stone industry in Mandalay is quite developed, but the business of judging stones is very difficult to describe. It can lead to wealth in the long run or poverty in the short run, but in the end, there are more who become rich. I saw a gray stone and asked about it. I was told that it was worth tens of thousands. It is said that emeralds are valued for their luster. The most expensive stones are ten times the price of gold. However, I heard that production has not been good in recent years, and the import tax from China has increased. Jade merchants are also complaining. However, the Chinese merchants have to transport the stones to Shanghai to make various utensils and then sell them to Europeans in Shanghai. I wonder why they don't sell them directly to Europe and save on import taxes, export taxes, and the involvement of foreigners. Mostly, Chinese people only know the Shanghai market and lack knowledge of the European and American markets. Also, because the local workers are clumsy, they have to be made in Shanghai factories because the Shanghai workers are clever. But I think it is better to move the workers here and save a lot of expenses.

Remembering My Three Friends in Hangzhou in the Cold Season by Huang Lu

Are you all well, pine, bamboo, and plum?

The weather is cold, and frost has settled; the year is coming to an end. I sigh at how quickly time passes and feel that my age is increasing in vain. In recent years, I have often been driven by food and clothing to travel north and south, and my body is like duckweed. Recently, I resigned from my reporting job in Hangzhou and came to Shanghai again. Although I am in the business world, I still cannot escape a writing life. In this time of severe frost, I cannot help but miss my three friends in Hangzhou. The three friends are the pines of Song's tomb road, the bamboo of Taoguang, and the plum blossoms of Gushan. Having more free time in my rented room, I picked up my pen to record this. If the three gentlemen knew, would they laugh at my foolish infatuation?

Song's tomb road is located behind Lingyin Temple, covering dozens of acres. There are more than a hundred levels of steps. The sides are planted with sparse pine trees, some gnarled and old like dragons, suitable for cranes to perch on, and some green and graceful, as tall as the clouds. Being in this place, quietly listening to the sound of the wind through the pines, echoing with the sound of the spring in the mountain stream, like the waves of a thousand acres, like the galloping of ten thousand horses, both majestic and grand, both elegant and secluded. I have lingered here for a long time, sighing, "If I could build a hut here in life and a tomb here in death, I would have no regrets for the rest of my life." But this wish will eventually become a dream.

From Lingyin to Taoguang, there are thousands of steps, with lush forests of bamboo on both sides. Those that are tall can be dozens of feet, and those that are short are also more than ten feet. The thick ones are like buckets, and the thin ones are like arms. From the foot of the mountain to the top, the total number should be in the tens of thousands. It cannot be said that it is not a grand sight. It is rumored that the bamboo for making Tianzhu chopsticks is taken from here, but in reality, it is not. Many visitors to Hangzhou like to carve their names on the bamboo stalks to leave a memento. An ancient poem says, "Thousands and thousands of bamboo stalks, only one or two plum blossoms." It can be believed that bamboo is best when in clusters and plum blossoms are best when sparse. Observing the seclusion of the Taoguang bamboo path further confirms this.

The plum blossoms of Gushan have been passed down for hundreds of years and are famous throughout the country. But in reality, they are sparse and not enough to be considered a grand sight. Hangzhou has many famous plum blossoms. For uniqueness and antiquity, the Tang plum and Song plum of Chaoshan are the best. For seclusion and elegance, the red plum and green calyx plum of Lingfeng are the best. The plum blossoms of Gushan are famous thanks to the talent of Lin Bu. Although the plum blossom is a noble recluse, it can only show its purity and integrity if it grows in a secluded valley and is not close to the world. The plum blossoms of Gushan, having no gardener to care for them and suffering the destruction of vulgar people, how can they not rot with other plants and trees?

Warmth on My Mind (339) by Bao Tianxiao

Episode 16: Courteously Asking for Words, Cuixiu Visits the Teacher; Generously Discussing Military Affairs, Famous Courtesans Banquet Female Heroes. In the end, is it Three Fives or Five Passes that are impassable? The third hand has already passed three passes, but these two passes cannot be passed no matter what. There is also a saying for playing Five Passes, called "Three Passes are easy, Two Passes are difficult." Luyi pushed the dominoes, pouted her cherry lips and said she wasn't playing anymore. Zuo Shichen smiled and said, "Let's play word association instead. This Five Passes game seems very mysterious. Sometimes you can pass it in one hand, and sometimes you can't pass it even if you play dozens of hands. You only know how to play Five Passes, but do you know the story behind Five Passes?" Luyi said, "Is there a story behind Five Passes?" Zuo Shichen said, "This is from the Romance of the Three Kingdoms. Cao Cao kept Guan Gong and wouldn't let him leave. He wanted to find his master Liu Bei, so he left Cao Cao's place, but he had to pass through five passes. The guards at the passes wouldn't let him pass without Cao Cao's orders. But Guan Gong relied on his martial prowess to seize the passes and leave. He passed through five passes and killed six of the guards before he could escape. This is called 'Five Passes, Slaying Six Generals.' Isn't there a method of slaying six generals in playing Five Passes?" Luyi said, "Then Cao Cao could have just not let Guan Gong leave, so why bother instructing the guards to stop him?" Zuo Shi said, "That's why Cao Cao is called a cunning hero. He used the method of pretending to let go in order to catch, and using someone else to kill. People say that Cao Cao treated Guan Gong so well, but when he left, he lost six generals, as if Guan Gong was being unreasonable." Luyi listened somewhat blankly and asked, "Is this all from the Romance of the Three Kingdoms?" Zuo Shichen said, "Of course. Fortunately, the guards Guan Gong encountered at the five passes were all incompetent. If there were one or two who were more skilled in martial arts than Guan Gong, then Guan Gong would be like you today." Luyi said, "How am I like you today?" Zuo Shichen smiled and said, "Like you, you can't pass the five passes today." Luyi said, "Comparing me to Guan Gong is a sin. It's a pity I can't read. If I could read and look at that novel, I could relieve my boredom." Zuo Shichen said, "Why don't you study? There are many ladies in their twenties and thirties who go to girls' schools. You're only sixteen this year, it's the perfect time to study." Her mother said, "Our girl did go to a school when she was thirteen. The teacher liked her very much, but she got sick and didn't go anymore. She only went to school for three months and read two textbooks. I'm afraid she's already returned them to the teacher." Zuo Shichen said, "Actually, you can study now. No matter what, it's always in your own interest to know more characters." Luyi sighed softly and said, "When I was at A Su's place, many guests also advised me to study, but someone who has eaten in a brothel is like a piece of pure white silk falling into a vat of dye."

"What's the point of studying anymore?"

American Cotton Suffers a Severe Blow

New York, 19th Report: The cotton market for the week ended with bullish sentiment. Southern hedge funds and banks were stranded. Weakness in the stock market led to near-month futures prices falling to 9.25 cents. However, they rebounded slightly due to inter-dealer buying to cover short positions and speculative buying. Based on current market prices, it can be determined that cotton fields will inevitably be abandoned. Even the economic situation in the South indicates a reduction in the use of fertilizers in the next season. However, industry insiders still have doubts about rising prices, believing that it depends on the development of real transactions. The chairman of the Agricultural Administration stated that the cotton market has now reached a point of severe pain. The 1.3 million bales stockpiled by the Maintenance Association and the 2 million bales held by the cooperative have the ability to accumulate for three years.
